Answer 	So knowledge is the ability to reliably accomplish something. It could be farming a field, it could be shooting a rocket to the moon. It is just the knowhow to accomplish some particular task and then if you can also then reliably share it, by talking or demonstrating in some way then that is knowledge that can be spread and that is how humanity has come out on top here on planet earth, at least so far.  I am we are not doing that creative a job, let’s be honest.  

Question 
Male	So how does scientific matter feed into that and what is, you know how?

Answer	How does the scientific method produce knowledge?  Yeah. So the scientific method produces knowledge in two ways. One it tests knowledge that may have been received like this is the best way to farm a field. Well there is a great way to test that, we can farm this field exactly that way and we can farm this other field in some other way. Look at the results and say, oh my gosh it turns out that field B works better where our received information was wrong. It also can produce knowledge by, you take hypothesis, again that would have been the farm field A is going to be good and you test it against reality.  Many multiple, multiple times. So let’s go to the big theory of evolution, that is an idea that Charles Darwin had, to explain a lot of observations that people have had. And then it was kind of tested against reality and seemed to work.  But what people don’t realise is that Charles Darwin didn’t really have a theory for how evolution worked and it took the discovery of genetics to really explain how you know we evolve and why.  And so that is kind of how science builds knowledge is taking an idea and testing it against it against reality and then finding out whether that is accurate or inaccurate.  

And you know one of the great things about science is that it is also always provisional. There is always a chance to improve. There is nothing that is finished, an end product. There is no end to knowledge. You can always kind of refine it further and get a little bit better whatever it might be.  And that can be quite daunting to people in that there is no like definitive end date or stop or you know ultimate idea. But to me it is actually quite beautiful. It is kind of getting ever, ever closer to the truth of this universe that we find ourselves in.  But never losing the wonder of really the miracle that is everything around us. And scientists are some of the most you know, they have a reputation as kind of these precise people, but they are actually quite artistic and full of kind of the joy of life. Because who better to be amazed by the workings of a cell than a biologist or convinced of the beauty of a jungle than an ecologist because they just have this extra knowledge of how it all works.

Answer
Male	Somebody who an atomic bomb was dropped on.  Yeah.

Question	Yes and they might have a different view.

Answer	Absolutely and I think even the scientists who were involved when they saw the first atomic bomb tests were not convinced of the rightness of the knowledge that they had uncovered. I mean there is certainly knowledge that is dangerous, right. And that is a prime example. It is hard to imagine what kind of the positive use of that particular tool is. So science often results in a technology. It could be your cellphone, it could be a hammer, it could be an atomic bomb.  And the reality of any tool or any technology is that it can be used for good.  You know a hammer can be used to hammer in a nail or it can be used for bad. A hammer can be used to hurt somebody.  Now unfortunately people seem to have an interest in developing technology for war and that is where kind of the atomic bomb was born and it was born out of kind of the pursuit of knowledge that had happened independently of that many years before in an attempt to understand what was going on in the stars, how physics actually worked, quantum mechanics and all the rest of it.  And then that knowledge was applied to a particular technology to unleash devastation.  That same knowledge maybe can be used more safely in say the discovery of a way to generate electricity from fusion which is what goes on in a star. Or perhaps I don’t know when we get to some future date to start our own star, should we need to, who knows.  

So I understand that not all scientific discoveries are kind of used for good. And I think we are in the midst of that in kind of the genetics realm right now. It is such an unclear science at this point and yet people are using it to determine peoples ethnic identity and to judge who is, who qualifies as a particular ethnic identity and who does not and sorting people never really ends well in history. So, but at the same time genetic information can be used to cure disease, it can be used to understand your history, your ancestry, it can give you answers, it can give you knowledge that other things can’t. So it is, in the end most of this comes back to the human problem which is how will we use this knowledge that we have and honestly, sometimes we will use it for ill, like the atomic bomb.

The scientific method seems deceptively simple but it is very hard to kind of get your own biocides out of it to accept what the data is telling you when it is telling you that, hey you thought farm field A was going to be great and it is actually farm field B. and you are like but wait a minute this is how we have been doing it for thousands of years. Question	Let’s just move slightly closer to education. Would you say that there is a move for values and some education is clearly acquiring knowledge. Perhaps has some pitfalls or situations that will lead to the wrong knowledge or produce not happy with?

Answer	Well I think one of the most important goals of education is kind of what is called in the US anyway, critical thinking, this is the ability to kind of evaluate multiple strands of evidence and come to some kind of conclusion in a world of grey. Or to figure out how to navigate a world of grey.

	So the great thing about science is it is concerned with the world of is. This is how the world is. And I can show you because I have this data to support this. Science has very little to say about the world of ought. Like we ought to do this because you know it is good for society. It is good for you, it is good for me or whatever it might be. Often times people want science to have more to say about aught. But that is not something that the scientific method is good for. And I actually think that is one of the greatest kind of misperceptions of some of the folks who really want to reject science as they feel like it is dictating what their values should be or whatever else. And science is not doing that unless their values are in some kind of rejection of the world around us and what you can observe for yourself which is very rarely the case because people like that don’t survive very long.  

	So you know we can have productive debates about what the values should be, what the ought should be. We can’t really have productive debates around what is.  And so you know I think that is kind of a big part of the challenge of understanding what kind of science is up to.  How you translate that into education is I think you. Well first of all you can certainly employ the scientific method a little bit to try to understand what works, what doesn’t work. But it can’t tell you what you ought to be teaching.  And that is something I think that everybody in a community or whoever is making the decision has to get together and do the hard work of hashing it out. This is you know what inspires us, this is what we believe this is what we want to pass onto the next generation. This is what we ought to teach, But certainly I would argue that one of the things we ought to teach is these critical thinking skills and the scientific method and some of the knowledge that has been produced in that way.

Question	It is change roles all the time and decide which one you like. That is what I do.

Let’s start. What is the purpose of TED talks?

Answer
Male	The purpose of TED talks is ideas worth spreading is the catch phrase. And as the science curator I tend to focus more on the worth than the spreading because to me it is more important that the ideas are worth something than that they are just kind of spreading willy nilly as we say in the US. And I think there is kind of an educational purpose obviously, certainly a lot of people use it that way. There is also a, I don’t know what the right phrase is, a self help aspect to TED talks. Often times people turn to them when they are looking for a change in their life or dealing with some problem and maybe there is a TED Talk that can speak to those issues. Of course the science TED Talks maybe don’t help with your personal life, but they do kind of expand your mind, introduce you to the wonder of the world maybe in a different way or just educate you about some possibility that you might not have heard about otherwise.

Question	You must work or some sort of working assumptions.  So what is your working assumption?

Answer	So specifically in the science domain I would say the ideas worth spreading are the ideas that have kind of stood some kind of test whether that is kind of an accuracy test, a peer review test, a Jury of your peers type test or just, and this is probably the most important test, an observational test, an imperial test. Those are the ideas that are worth spreading.

04:45:24	You know, the best part of being the science curator is I don’t have to worry about politics that much and that is where you really get into situations where spreading can overwhelm worth. 

	So how I pick science speakers is I basically just look for the most amazing thinkers who have the most intriguing idea and then try to convince them to get up on stage in a little red circle which is not typically what scientists want to do.  And so the best part of my job is being a perpetual student in that way and having conversations with these brilliant people and sometimes it works out and it is great. Sometimes there is a TED talk and then maybe didn’t go so well. And sometimes there isn’t actually a TED talk there, right. We have some dialogue and you know you realise that this person or this idea is not the exact right one for a TED talk.

Question	So how does that work?  You hand pick scientists?

Answer	Yeah. So you know I am going around everywhere including Bangladesh looking for folks with intriguing ideas who are working in kind of scientific domain. So that might be I see some paper you published in a journal. It might be that I am at a conference, in a boring windowless room you know with stuffy air. But you are able to kind of tell this captivating story of how you did your science. Or it might be word of mouth right, like somebody says, some Nobel prize winners like, oh you really need to pay attention to this particular chemist, and then I will pay attention to that particular chemist. So that is probably 70-80% of it. We do also accept public submissions and people will  kind of go through that and surface the best ones.  And then I guess the final way that people get a science TED talk anyway is getting involved in our TED fellows or TED prize programmes where you know we try to help your dreams become reality. That is where is some actual money put behind the TED talk.  

Question	You are saying that you can avoid politics, but your politics is believe in size and it is positive and you need to put a spotlight on people who are heroes that few.  But tell me more about it, your belief?

Answer	[Laughing]

Question	In the context of technology?

Answer	For me it is not that I have a belief in scientists or any particular idea, except for one which is this method, the scientific method which is just a great way of testing what you want to believe against reality.  And that is really what it comes down to. And the best scientists recognise how often they are going to fail and honestly that is in a way why science has become politicised because it is very easy to say, point it at climate change and see all the doubts and uncertainties and all the usual characteristics of good science. And we’re like well then, I just will choose not to believe that. But of course thermometers are not republican or democrat, they just read the temperature and if the temperature is going up, oh well  then maybe global warming is happening. I would suggest it is.
04:51:04
	So I don’t know. That is how I deal with that. And so I try to employ this idea of the scientific method in my selection process and that is something that I think is truly one of those kind of foundational ideas where it is spreading and maybe could be usefully applied in some other areas of life.  

Question	But if again, taking the broader area, it is a conviction. There is a sort of conviction of ignorance as a never get thing from our lives. And scientific ideas are something that actually help with that, well not help. We are at a guess are the exact opposite of ignorance. So in that sense would you say that TED Talk is educational and solution that tries to dissipate ignorance?

Answer	Absolutely. I think it is not just about dissipating ignorance, it is also about trying to spread real change in the world, right. If you are able to kind of give some amazing person who has for example some great idea of how to solve the last mile problem in health care which could save you know millions of lives around the world, and you are able to give them a platform like TED Talks to spread that idea and to reduce the ignorance that is kind of causing this problem, that is causing people to die.  That is you know a huge privilege. So absolutely that is what I am hoping to do. I mean obviously we are not always doing that. Sometimes it is just hey look at these cool pretty pictures of algae, like did you know how cool algae were or blind cave fish or whatever else it might be. And that is a really cool TED talk too, because you know you might have thought, hey what do blind cave fish have to do with my life. But they really kind of teach you about this other idea, evolution which turns out to be important in understanding the world around us.  

And in addition, it is just fun to kind of share in the individual scientists passion for that particular thing, right. So somebody who has devoted their life to the study of blind cave fish really has an unusual enthusiasm for these fish that maybe nobody else thinks about. And if they can infect you with that, that also is helpful in combating ignorance.  

Question	And curiosity is there?

Answer	Yes I agree and certainly people are naturally curious.  You know there is the old saying that curiosity killed the cat. But I think that really applies more in kind of the I don’t know social setting.  Curiosity is you know you absolutely must have it if you are going to be a scientist or employing the scientific method.  And I think that is what unites scientists or makes them equally human to artists or whoever else.  I mean we often treat.  

04:55:38	One of the other things I try to accomplish as TED Science Curator is to demystify science. Because I feel that people feel it is done by people who are much smarter than them or have different skills than them or some kind of elite mandarin type of people. And it is not true, they are actually just like you and me and they just are employing their scientific method in a particular way to try to learn or get closer to some truth about the world. And I think once people kind of see the humanity of scientists that will maybe change some of the political challenges that science and scientists have faced.

Question	So what is knowledge?

Answer	What is knowledge?  Wow, that is a very profound question.  What is knowledge?  I don’t know that I have ever had to think about what is knowledge before. It is just kind of one of those assumed things. But I guess if I had to put it into words, knowledge is the ability to reliably accomplish something whether that is knowing that you are, how your camera works and how to make it work. Or how to farm a field or how to start a fire. How to shoot a rocket to the moon. Those are all forms of knowledge that are kind of up here and then can be shared, this thing that is flapping in front of you, between people. And that way kind of infects the world. That is, I don’t know, that is how I think about knowledge. You might have a better answer. 

Question	Are you able to repeat it word for word?

Answer	Absolutely not [laughing]  But I can answer the question again.

They take weeks on a particular topic and they dip into it once they have gone deep enough. And in the next one or two weeks they change the subject and they have unanswered questions that just keep unanswered questions and later children wonder what the answer or solution to it can be.

SADAF SAAZ, DIRECTOR OF LIT FEST
Dhaka Lit Fest, November 2018
01:56:00	[Break]

Male	Can you give me your name and tell me in general terms about [?] what it is?

Sadaf Saaz	So my name is Sadaf Saaz, I am Director and Producer of Taka LitFest. The festival is I would say an amazing literary and cultural adventure.  We started it in 2011 in a very kind of small way, about 600 people. It has grown into a massive event with thousands attending. Many of them very young people from all over Bangladesh.  And it has really I think grown into a place where there is debate, conversation on all kinds of topics from poetry to philosophy. Fiction to current affairs and we also have amazing performances from different regions in Bangladesh. We highlight the different languages, apart from Bangla. And it is just a really great place for people to come together and have real conversations about things that matter to us. 

Question	Can you talk to us a little bit about the role of festivals like this in the role of culture?

Answer	The reason why we started the festival was, well we felt that we were very cut off from the kind of global scene. Nobody really knew much about Bangladesh. And Bangladesh is a very rich and varied cultural and literary history. Our written forms of literature go back to the 18-12th century. In fact some of the original Buddhist texts which were taken to Tibet came from these old Buddhist poems that were written in Proto Bangla.  We have always had a very kind of, and of course the oral forms are coming out in very different ways.  Imbibe and assimilate the pluralism and syncretism I think of many of the great religions that have kind of come and been practiced here side by side.  For example Buddhism, Hinduism, Islam, Christianity and Animism.  And so I think we are a product of that and this kind of history of tolerant thinking, of diverse thinking of imbibing all sorts of different kinds of ways of thinking is very much part of our history. And we really felt that a platform was needed to sort of take our history and culture to the rest of the world as well as our contemporary writing and engagement with poetry and writing and fiction and provide a platform to the rest of the world. 

But we also felt it was very important for the great thinkers and writers to come here and our young people to be exposed to different ideas and different ways of thinking and different perspectives.  Because this is basically very much part of how we have evolved as a country and as a society.  

And so that was kind of the idea behind the LitFest.  After starting the LitFest, especially in recent years it has become much more urgent to keep this space for creative thinking, an open space to basically have the space to be able to sort of debate and inquire about things that are happening around us.  In a kind of world where these spaces are shrinking everywhere and the internet sometimes is kind of more constricting rather than broadening our horizons. We felt it was time to sort of have a place where people could actually converse with each other and open their minds to different narratives. 
02:00:00
And that is what we try and do at the LitFest. To basically have a range of topics, diverse topics where people can kind of hear other peoples point of views. Hear the way other people think. And you know basically use that to help create and express how we ourselves think. And I think that is really important for kind of the education we are giving our children. And it is really important for young people to be exposed, not just a very kind of narrow type of education that we have kind of inherited form the kind of colonial era. But it is important I think for young people to not just be on their electronic devices and in their own echo chambers. But actually realise there is a whole world out there.

The other thing is that you know we wanted young people to be exposed to the greatest minds, to see what people are thinking and to have that freedom and the confidence to follow their own thoughts. But to be able to have the building blocks to do so.  And you know we are I think the strength of Bangladesh I think when anybody comes here feels there is something wonderfully intangible that gives us that confidence to go out into the rest of the world to be tolerant to other people’s ideas and respectful of other people’s ideas. But still have the confidence to have our own convictions. And I think when young people come here and go to a diverse range of topics, many of them may not have even thought of going or have been exposed to them. I mean I could go to you know London and New York and you know pay 50 dollars or 80 dollars to go and see a session. But I have that privilege. There are many young people here who don’t have that chance. And for them to go to a lecture and over the past years often I have had people come up and say that going to a session has been life changing for them. They have heard an author say something that has completely changed the direction of what they feel that they can do with their life, has completely realigned what they felt was potential within themselves.

MADIHA MURSHED, SCHOLASTICA AND AURORA SCHOOLS
DHAKA LIT FEST, NOVEMBER 2018

Male	Tell me your name and tell me about the school?

Answer
Madiha Murshed
	I am Madiha Murshed.  And I actually run two schools. The larger of the two schools, the more established one is called Scholastica.  It is a school that my mother founded over 40 years ago. It is a private school. We teach in English. We teach the British curriculum so the O and A levels. And it is a pre-K through 12 school. It is a very, very large school. We have over 5,000 students spread out in different campuses throughout the city.  

	I also run much smaller international school that I founded about four years ago, that is much smaller, just about 50 students and we are hoping to teach an international curriculum and that is just in one location in the city.   

Question	And what is the difference, you said that the main school is more traditional?

Answer	Yes exactly it is a more traditional school. It depends on how you use the word traditional. I don’t mean that it is a conventional teaching method. We are definitely trying to improve the way that we teach. Basically the way education is in Bangladesh it was very, and continues to a large extent to be very book learning, memorisation, book based. And over the last 15-20 years we have been trying to break out of that and really sort of make our teaching more student centred, more hands on, more experiential for our students. Having said that, with the larger school, with Scholastica, that is definitely a work in progress. I can’t see that we have achieved that at all. We have definitely begun trying and I think we are doing that to some extent, but it is usually two steps forward one step back.

Question	And the international school is different?

Answer	Yes

Question	So how exactly, the model of the international school and how is it different?

Answer	So the international school, I guess we started it, our management team started it because the ideas we wanted to have a school where we teach the way we want to teach if you know what I mean, to really teach the way we think education should be.  The model is very simple. It is really just also the student centred teaching. We hope to have an international curriculum we will be applying to be accredited by an international organisation. But for now really it is about. So right now the school is only up to grade 1. And at the pre-school level it is all sort of learning through play. And we don’t emphasise academics, we emphasise skill building. So emotional and physical and you know social skills, personal skills. All of those kinds of things. And once they come into Grade 1, that is when the academics start. 

So it is different really. It is not really different so much in philosophy, it is different in practice because it is a very small school, hand-picked teachers. So we are actually able to walk the walk.  You know what I mean.

Question	So what are the principles?  You said I pick up on words, you said the way we want. So describe this philosophy because you said, what I was hearing was that you carefully pick teachers to share your vision and so what exactly is this vision?

Answer	So I think for me as an educator what I struggle with and I was saying this to Bill a little while ago. I understand that we as educators often tend to teach children to prepare them for a world that we live in which is not necessarily the world that they will be living in 20 years from now, 30-40 years from now. And I think our job as a educator has become all the harder now because I can’t even fathom what that world will look like. 

02:15:00	I can’t fathom what their jobs will be, I have no idea. Very few people probably do. So how do you prepare young people for skills that you and for an environment, a working environment and a social and political environment that you can’t really imagine.

	So what we have tried to do is ensure that, especially you are asking me about my principles. The principles are really about trying to give the students whatever skills we think they need so that whatever comes at them they will be able to adapt and learn and strive.  And what does that mean?  So as I said, we are really trying to make it hands on, we try and ensure that our students, that it is coming from a place of their own curiosity and then that they are given the freedom to explore and nurture their curiosity.  Of course there is a structure. I think every school needs to have a certain amount of structure and you do need to be teaching academics because if you don’t there isn’t a context for the world. 

You need science, you need history, you need geography. But you can teach it in a way which is experiential and where they are learning for themselves rather than being told. And putting two and two together rather than being told that two plus two equals four if you know what I mean. So we are trying to make it much more about the students developing whatever skills they need so that they can keep learning into the future. Assuming that there will be, I mean who knows 20 years from now maybe all of us will have to learn some new programming language or you know what I mean, whatever it is, we have to make sure they will be able to learn. That they, when they are 30 years old they are still being able to learn and pick up a new skill or adapt to whatever the world is.  

	At the same time I feel a responsibility also to ensure that our students are thoughtful, productive, contributing members of society. So really instilling in them a sense of responsibility, talking to them about what their responsibilities are. So focusing on things like character education, making sure. I worry a lot about media literacy these days. I worry about all the information that all of us have at our fingertips to the point where you no longer need to really be sharing knowledge with students right.  You don’t need, they need to understand, they need to be to analyse and critical of history. But they don’t need to know particular data, they can just Google it.  Rather what is more important is when they Google it and they get 10,000 articles, which ones are true, what is fact, what is truth, what is fact with opinion and how do you make sense of all that. How do you think critically about all that and how do you form your own opinions based on what you are reading.  

I think now more than ever. I mean I can give you many examples of why I feel like that, it is really, really important for our students to be able to do. And for me a lot of that means also to make knowledge for them to be film making and learning about photography and learning about it. Because if they are not doing it themselves then how will they be able to differentiate between doctored photographs and not for example if you know what I mean.  

So those are all kind of part of the philosophies basically and efforts to think about what skills our students need going into the future and then trying to build that into the design of the school and the design of our curriculum.

Question 	A particular question, it might sound vague, but actually what is a school?

Answer	As an institution, yeah

Question	As a place, what do you as a person?

Answer	That is a great question. I think it is to prepare young people, well maybe in two ways. One is to give them the chance to interact with their peers in a structured setting. I think that is really important. I think if we didn’t have schools, if young people were just growing up you know in their own homes and in their own communities, I am not sure there would be that kind of, the interaction amongst peers and I think it would be really healthy to sort of not only in terms of friendships but in terms of challenging you and shaping your character and moulding who you are and what your interests are and all that.

	But I think it is cool also, it is a place for young people to become themselves, to figure out who they are and for me a big part of it how they are going to, what their place is in society.  How will they contribute to society. I want to actively encourage our young people to be contributors not just taking but contributing, giving back in whatever way.  There are so many ways one can do that. So I think a school is a place that young people can do that, find themselves and then figure out who they are going to be and what they are going to be going forward.

I think some people will find themselves, they can sit under a tree for 40 years and find themselves. For a lot of other people that isn’t necessarily the case. I think you have to ask questions, you have to provoke thought. You have to build skills. And I think, and that is what I mean. I think that a school can do that, which if they were left to their own devices at home may or may not happen.

Question	Tell me a little bit about the, I am hearing that Bangladesh has a kind of expectation, quite conservative expectations in education. Answer	Yes I would say almost the majority of parents in this country care about education.  And actually I would say that there is a really, there is a premium on education. People prioritise education. I have seen a lot of families sacrifice a lot to get their child the best possible education they can. So I think there is a real respect for education. But yes exactly I think there is by and large, I am making a generalisation, but by and large parents see education as a way to you know guarantee a certain standard of living for their children. And as you said, a certain social status for their children. They don’t by and large they don’t see it as person building, it is more like. This is what you need so that you can get a good job. So it is a very practical kind of look on education.

	And the problem with that is as a consequence many parents, obviously not all, but many parents don’t really even value the education, they just value that certificate. So as long as my child is getting the A’s or they are passing whatever exam they have to take and they are getting into medical school and passing their medical exams and becoming a doctor, that is all that matters. Whether they are a good doctor or not, whether they have learned, whether they have become a good person or not, whether they can think critically and all those sorts of things, are less important. In some cases less even understood.

02:25:02	And they can get through it in a way that makes them stronger. I actually think that is a specific skill you know. And you teach those in all different kinds of ways. You teach it in the classroom, you teach it by modelling as a teacher. You teach it in terms of talking to students in all the different contexts in which they are, not just in the classroom but even when they are playing with their friends and things like that. 02:30:00	So when you talk about student centre teaching, when you talk about hands on learning, not only have they never seen it, they can’t fathom it. They don’t know what that looks like. And they don’t understand why it would be better or what the value is in it.

11:44:17
Question
Female	So Nicholas please talk to me about learning, what you think of when you think of learning?

Answer
Nicholas	Well when I think of learning I think about learning, learning because I am less interested in what kids or even adults know versus their ability to learn.  And this has obviously become much more important because as you go through life the opportunity to learn more and your life changes especially as the next generation starts to live to 150 and maybe 200 years old. The idea that you are going to learn in the first twelve years what you need for the next 180 years is kind of silly.

	So learning, learning has been the mantra of the media lab, this is what we have done since our inception and before.  Tried to look at how you could enable kids to learn how to learn. And it turns out there is a way. And one of the best approximations for thinking is writing a computer programme. And the reason that is true is indeed an approximation that you are taking apart and creating an algorithm a sort of way of describing what you want done. You execute the programme and usually it does not do what you want to do. And it does something else. In the digital world doing something else is not just that it stops.  Let’s say you want to draw a circle and what comes on the screen are lots of random lines. You use the behaviour of the machine to help you debug the programme which is a very good approximation of learning itself. So it turns out we could prove this. That kids who write computer programmes at an early age, maybe 4,5 and 6 years old are better at learning. And even though it is a bit abstract to say well they looked at and taught ‘a machine’ and as a consequence they know more about learning is actually true.  And one of the very early phenomenon and I am talking about 1970s, late 1970s when my dear friend Seymour Papird and I we put some computers in schools in Harlem. Now they were not little mini computers they were pretty big computers and the kids it was their lab and they used it and the kids who used the lab and wrote computer programmes were better spellers. They spelt better and people say wait a minute why are those kids spelling better because spelling has nothing to do with computer programming.

Female	And it is a code?

Nicholas	It is but what was it about spelling. And I will tell you exactly what it was. Most kids at most schools that grade and have tests punish you for the words you get wrong. So let’s say it is a spelling B and you have ten words and if you get eight right. And the two that you get wrong are the ones you put under the rug. Because you have been punished for them. You might take notice and [?] with them next time. But you really find no joy in those two words.  

In computer programming the most fun that the kids have is debugging. So what did those kids do when they had a spelling B?  They  would go to each other and they would say what two words did you get wrong? And you said, I spelled receive wrong. So no silly you, don’t you know it is ‘i’ before ‘e’ except after ‘c’.  Oh I forgot that and they talk about it, they play with it. They joke about the errors and in that process those kids really became better spellers because of the joy and playfulness with which they dealt with the wrong words.  And again that sounds a bit abstract but it is actually true.

And they learn all their science through this procedure. They learn all their weights and measures and resins and whatever buoyancy and everything.  But it is incredibly important it is done as a class and then at the end you sail it across our bay. And if you have done it wrong you will sink as a class. But that is a very. One might say a luddite example. But to transpose that attitude and confidence to coding is very inspiring. 

Nicholas	And the confidence that may come from doing the canoe or debugging a programme is.  Would it be because you know you know it is because you are willing to explore and it is a little bit like young children learning languages. They are out there, they are trying things and you realise that the errors aren’t a problem at all but that is actually the way you have learned.

And one of the countries has no tests, has no competition as we would think of it in most schools. And now there are people in this building who want to grow buildings from seeds.  So you plant a seed and a building grows. So you say that is ridiculous, it doesn’t make any sense. Well it doesn’t make any sense today just like other things didn’t make sense 20 years ago.  So it will make sense in part or in whole or maybe there will be derivatives. Maybe you will find that we are more Cartesian than we want to believe and people would be uncomfortable living in a world of low resolution edges and curves and so on which nature naturally makes.  That there would be alternates or hybrids of this. But the idea that you can grow things that you can genetically modify things, in ways never considered before is a huge difference.

	So art and science I mean there have been Leonardo De Vinci’s for years. But you never thought of that being the same as people who would understand the natural sciences, biology and the fact that that and engineering are now the same. It really gets rid of all the boundaries.

Female	And then my next question would be, where do these free thinkers, how to make sure they are not over educated, over tested, over demoralised out of this imaginative space and imaginative capacity?

Answer
Nicholas	Well you know each country does it its own way. Family does it its own way.  Education is what you do to somebody and learning is what you do to yourself. And as let’s say a government or a group of people who want their kids to learn better, you could create a system which is then called education in a variety of different ways. And as that progresses you tend to, governments do this all the time, is to optimise for the system. So something as simple as grades.  By grades I don’t mean scores, a,b,c. I mean for a second, third grade. The idea of having a grade is not an intellectual decision that has to do with how we learn, it is in fact a convenience. 

Female	An industrial decision?  

Nicholas	And we are going to take all the six year olds, we will put them in one group. We will take the seven year olds and then we will pretend that they have to learn certain things before other things which is more often than not untrue. And it is you know we compartmentalise and then we give them scores because that is another way of moving forward. And all of this is optimised for the system not for learning. And it is often done at the expense of learning.

Question
Female	So what do you see as the next challenge for a society that is engaging with our digital capacities in terms of learning, in terms of learning rather than teaching?

Answer
Nicholas	The next frontier has actually already here, it is just it is right in front of us and we don’t you know necessarily include it.  And that is the degree to which children today can play with things that are much closer to learning. We say well they shouldn’t be on their computers and they shouldn’t be using their tablets.  Well that is not necessarily true.  And we have found when we did experiments in African villages and throughout the rest of the world, villages that had zero literacy, we found that the kids became so fascinated that the proudest moment I have had, is when the work we were doing in these developing countries led to the children teaching their parents how to read and write. And when that happens once, ten times, a hundred times, a thousand times, you say wow that is pretty interesting. And the relationship between the child and the parent didn’t deteriorate because the parent didn’t suddenly lose you know the ability to discipline or whatever, but it made a much stronger bond. And that happened over and over and over again. And in situations that a particular experiment we ran, the children prior to introducing and this case it was tablets into a village that had no schools, no literacy, no nothing.  The kids their job was to go and fetch water which could be a few miles away.  And they were delighted to do that and rolled these barrels back and that was the water supply system.

	Tablets come along and the kids were spending 7-8 hours a day on the tablet, not fetching water. And we thought, oh my goodness this is really. Nobody is going to like this. The parents were perfectly fine. They didn’t know why, in other words it was not as if they completely understood what was going on, but they watched their kids doing things and they said, okay well we will fetch the water for now. And there is a sort of innate belief that curiosity that the kids have and of course the parents had. So once the kids become in some parts of the world, the agents of change, it is a very different kind of learning and a very different esteem that kids have. And that self esteem self propels other things.

And if most of those jobs don’t exist because they are if you will sub-human, that maybe a really good thing not a bad thing. And most people don’t think about it that way. They think about this engine that needs fuel and education creates the fuel for this engine. And you then pour the kids into the engine that keeps it turning and at some point, depending on how lucky you were, you may then exit the other end and at some age where you probably can’t even appreciate it anymore because you are a little feeble, you get to sit back and enjoy those benefits if you will. That is a very funny way to think of the world. And if you really did think the assumption that computers and robots could do anything and moreorless everything, then what is it that humans can do. And we have precedent or we have a lot of precedent in Europe in the 17th, 18th, 19th century where aristocrats and royalty didn’t work at all, they did basically nothing, but they did listen to music and they wrote books and they read to each other and some decided poetry. It was a very exclusive sub-set of the world. But then most people and I think fair to say everybody in this lab doesn’t think of themself as having a job. But if you do it for other reasons and how many people can that extend? And in theory you should be able to extend to everybody doesn’t have to be. Just a limited sub-set of the world.

And her father said, you are lucky because tonight our cow is giving birth. And the light on her camera on it. And said you can stay up and basically film, video the cow’s birth. Which the little girl brought it back to class. When everybody showed their projects, she showed the birth of the cow. And the entire class was so fascinated with the birth of the cow that as a group they decided to upload the video to You Tube. Which is not trivial. They did it and the cow video got a few million hits within a few days. 

Now the important part of the story is what I haven’t told you and that is that the girl was at the bottom of the class by normal measures.  Was suddenly you know the hero for that moment. And the teacher said, wow I never thought that one of my little homework assignments might be viewed by two billion people. So everybody in that sort of got a different view of what they were doing. And the little girl was you can imagine went on for the next few years to do better and better and better in school by just that one incident which triggered the confidence and inspiration.  And it is anecdotes like that that make me deeply believe the way to think of learning and education. And the drill and practice measurement of oriented systems that most of us in the west apply, is just, is a fatal mistake, but everybody is doing it. And even if you persuade somebody that maybe there is an alternate which maybe you are successfully doing, most parents say, well I don’t want to risk it with my kid.

Male	Can you just explain the protocol and rationale and how links with [?] digital tools in education, what is the rationale?

Answer
Nicholas
12:25:05	So I had been running the media lab for about 20 years and decided it was time for somebody else to do that. And at the time I sort of had a home in Switzerland and a home in Greece and I thought perfect I will retire and spend the winters in one place and the summers in another.  This was about 15, almost 20 years ago. And I said, no instead what I should do as I know all the people who have given lots of financial support to the media lab, let me do one last big thing. And Seymour Papire was alive at the time and we started the one laptop per child programme which started off as a very technical solution to how do make 100 dollar laptop? Because what was happening in the commercial world was that companies like Microsoft were making faster and faster software systems and companies like Intel were making faster and faster processors. But the one was eaten by the other so the net net people using it was basically zero. And even if that is not perfectly accurate it is an approximation of what was going on. And the price was at a thousand dollars constantly. So we said, what if you could really change that equation and change. And as we were working on that and the idea that this being laptop for children you could drop from 20ft, it was waterproof, it worked in the sun, you can hand crank it, it was a tablet as well as a laptop and had lots of techie features that we loved and thought we knew a lot about. And it would be a laptop kids could use to particular write computer programmes.

	And as it evolved as a non profit, separate from the media lab.  I took a leave of absence from MIT, a new director was found that I literally went across the street to a building just across the street and we grew to about a hundred people. At first the hardware and software and then going out into the field which typically locals. And in three years we were able to build and ship three million laptops to countries around the world mostly Latin America, but let’s say two thirds there and one third in Africa. And as it grew we found certain countries would adopt it with open arms and others would reject it like India rejected it and others. China rejected it. And so there if you will, educational sort of didn’t want to embrace it.  

	Now three million laptops if I were starting a business and told you I had a business plan to make three million laptops and sell them in the first three years, that is a pretty good business. But it was non profit and we were funded by very many of the same people who had been funding the media lab. And was able to grow that rapidly. But what really happened with one laptop per child is something that nobody ever got to know or follow. And that is by the time we built our three million laptops it was pretty clear to people we could build laptops, we had a factory in Taiwan, that made the prototypes and major factory on mainland China. Now they weren’t devoted to us, it was a huge company, they made most people’s laptops. But we could push the button so to speak and generate 100,000 per week of our laptops and ship them by sea to wherever you wanted them at very low cost where you never got down to quite a hundred, but depending on currencies you could maybe get to a hundred and twenty or a hundred and fifty.  Also the cost of oil, all sorts of things were contained in that number. And we were always dealing with the Head of State and in the case of Brazil [?] was in power and I said to him I have an idea, because he was about to issue a tender for million laptops. You can’t just call up your buddy Nicholas and say I want a million laptops. There are laws, there are tenders. And I said, let me help you write the tender, not because I never write my laptop [?] but I know enough about the field and I promise you not to write my laptop. And we you know the tenders we put out were bid, but we will do is bid publically, publish it in the newspaper. Two weeks before it is due we will put our price, which nobody ever does, everyone keeps that as a secret and then they all bid and the lowest price wins. So we publish our price in the Brazilian newspapers and in that particular tender was 179 dollars which included training and spare parts and so 179 per laptop. And the winner got it for 180. We published our own price so they knew, they had to be a dollar more or maybe it was even 179.50 cents, but it was very small delta. And when that happened and they got the million laptops I realised wow what a great solution because we can keep publishing our price which are honest prices. We had perfect credibility because not just [?] but others, now we can push that button and generate them. And we can drive all the prices way down. And so the number of laptops that we distributed was 3.5 or some relatively small number, but we were won by the others as a number like 40-50 million. And so that was the great accomplishment at least on the economic side of that to push the prices.  Which we could never do if we had not built the first three [?]. You can’t just arrive and publish a price so we had to deliver the first ones. And that part of the story has basically never been told, but you know again it had anecdote stories and they are very if you are photogenic, the cow type story and people pick up from those. And it has had historically, I have never been involved in something where hindsight, sort of 20 years later actually is more positive than it was at the time. At the time it was really not an appreciated project and many things went wrong. And there was you see this, you see that. And it was subject to a great deal of criticism.  And now almost 20 years later people think of it as this great project and look what it did. And at the time it was pretty frustrating. We were being crucified in places for doing it, not necessary for the right reasons.

To the extent the cost of the laptop was the price of the laptop and it would vary from laptops. MITCH RESNICK AND TILDA
MIT Media Lab, May 2019

Female	Just start, go for it.  
12:40:00
Male	I think one of the real problems in education is that people too often think about learning in terms of a type of delivery mechanism. You are delivering information from a teacher to a student and the process of education is seen as how can we improve the delivery of information from teacher to student and this emphasis on making it more efficient and deliver that information. But for me learning is not about delivering information.  For me learning is a process of an individual developing new ways of seeing the world through exploring and experimenting and expressing themselves. And of course they interact with other people with teachers and others in order to help them explore, experiment and express themselves. But it is not about the learner taking in information. And in fact information is not at the core of it. The point is not just gathering lots of information, but developing a better understanding of the world, of yourself through a constant interaction with others. Actually it is a little bit like an analogy with the way media works these days. It used to be seen as broadcast media. You would broadcast information to a viewer. And you would think much more about an interactive style of interaction with media.  And learning the same way is a matter of learning through our interactions with the  world. So how it [?] trying to see how is it we can support those types of interactions with the world to help children and people of all ages better explore, experiment and express themselves. 

And I think that is maybe that is more important today than ever before because the world is changing so quickly. Any particular information you learn it might be outdated or outmoded by the time kids grow up. Just gathering information is certainly not a good strategy any more.  We know that today’s kids as they grow up are going to be confronted with a never ending stream of unknown and uncertain and unpredictable situations because things are changing so quickly. So what is going to be most important for today’s kids is the ability to think and act creatively. To come up with innovative approaches to the unexpected things they undoubtedly will encounter in their lives.  So always trying to think how can we support that creative learning. And I hope if I was around a hundred years ago or two hundred years ago I would still have been in favour of creative learning.  Kids learn to think creatively, act creatively. But it is even more important today than ever before. And we know that just delivering information is not going to be the right way to help kids to develop as creative learners. So in our work we are always thinking how can we support that type of creative learning approach. And I think it is the way we try and take seriously, here at the media lab where I work with big kids, university students, with researchers, we think it is important to be creative learners here. So at a place like the media lab we arrange it so that people are constantly being able to not just work on leading edge technologies, but do it creatively and innovatively and come up with new ideas to spread to the world. 

And it makes us frustrated when we go down the street to look at elementary school and we don’t see kids having the same type of creative learning opportunities and too often kids are still sitting at desks, listening to lectures, filling out work sheets. And it is not that they don’t learn anything from doing that, they aren’t developing as creative thinkers. And so they aren’t really preparing for what is really needed in today’s society. And we are saying needed in today’s society. I mean not just for the workplace, where it is certainly needed for the workplace, but also in your own personal life to be able to navigate an ever changing world. And participate in your local communities with your family, your friends, your community. How to be able to actively participate in the world around you. We need kids to grow up as creative thinkers. 
12:46:06
	As we have thought about how is it we can help kids grow up as creative thinkers? We have been especially inspired by the way the children learn in kindergarten. You know we think the traditional kindergarten gets kids get off to a good start. That in the traditional kindergarten kids do spend a lot of time experimenting, exploring designing, creating, they build towers with blocks, make pictures with finger paints and crayons. And in the process they learn a lot. They build a tower with blocks, they learn about structure and stability, what makes things stand up, fall down and they make a picture with finger paints they learn how colours mix together. But even more important I think they learn about the creative process, how to start with an idea, to try out the idea, to share the idea with others, to get feedback and ideas to experiment and to try new things. To have things not work out and then make adjustments to improve it. So iterative cycle of constantly imagining new things. Trying to it out in the world, getting feedback from others, experimenting and that sparks new ideas. And we see that happening in the traditional kindergarten but we think that should be for learners of all ages. So we are trying to take that approach that has been successful in kindergarten and extent it to learners of all ages. And that is why I call my research group the lifelong kindergarten group.  So it is for learners of all ages should have that same type of kindergarten approach to learning. 

Question
Female	And I am thinking of your example of going into an elementary school where children are not given the license to have this, there isn’t the patience and understanding to have this free space. And of course that is down to their teachers and school boards and parents not having confidence in it and having had a different education themselves.  So we know that children are eminently and everlastingly flexible and resourceful, we know that. And give them that free space and they will encounter being bored or being challenged or being over excited with all sorts of vim and vigour. But it is adults or people who have been brought up in a different way who I am really interested in looking at now.  I mean obviously we can’t just sit around and wait for three year olds to develop to the point where because we haven’t got that much time, it would be nice to think it is possible to re-educate or re-engage people who have had a different experience.  What would you say about that?
12:50:05
Answer	In fact if we could wait just for today’s three year olds to grow up and to change the world to be honest I am willing to wait, because I think this is a long term effort, but I worry that those three year olds are going to get influenced by the current system and they will be changed by the time they become 15 year olds, 25 year olds, 45 years. So we need to change the overall environment the kids are growing up in.  It is a difficult challenge, I sometimes say that we need to change two things that are difficult to change. We need to change mindsets and structures. We need to change mindsets the way that people think about educational learning. As long as people think about educational learning as a delivering mechanism of delivering information to kids then we are not going to change things.

	Certainly we need to change the structures of school systems and other educational environments as well. Because often they are set up in a way that makes it very difficult for kids to continue to develop as creative thinkers. If we set up schools where their 50 minute time periods and then they have to move onto the next thing. Or one week curriculum unit and then move onto the next thing. If we set up in school where each discipline is segregated from one and other of kids of different ages are segregated from one and other. If schools are separate from community. All those types of barriers and divisions make it very difficult for kids to grow up as creative thinkers.

	Now those things are hard to change, they are built into our systems and often it is hard to change one little piece without disrupting other parts. But those types of changes we do need, we need to make those changes eventually. So I think there is both a short term and a long term. We can start making small examples of how we can make changes and to highlight them to understand new possibilities. But this has to be a long term effort. I sometimes say that I am a short term pessimist and long term optimist. Because I know how difficult change is, that makes me a short term pessimist. We can’t expect everything to change over night because mindsets and structures are hard to change. But I am certainly a long term optimist because I know this alternative approach to learning education is what children need. And I think overall society will recognise that over time because the society is changing in a way that we need to start dealing with educational learning in different ways. So I definitely believe we are moving in the right direction and we see some very promising examples.   We can’t see great examples but inside schools and outside of schools they are trying new things and succeeding and helping children develop as creative thinkers and we need to highlight those examples and continue to that those children as they grow older as they can continue to help bring about those changes as they get older. 

Question	And to up the short term pessimism a little we can also say that the outdated modes are crashing, they are not serving society well and mental health and a general state of societal alienation is what we see now. And we are pretty clear that these delivery system education models are largely to blame?

Answer	I totally agree that the current system is not working and more people are recognising that. We need to get a broader understanding of both why it is not working and what the alternatives are.  Because if we don’t agree where we are headed, we are not likely to get there. And for me the starting point is to help get a better understanding of what should be the goals of learning and education because if people continue to think about education about learning a specific set of facts and skills to prepare you for particular jobs that is not going to be a successful strategy.  But in my mind the goal of education is to help children grow up as creative thinkers so they are able to actively participate in all parts of their lives whether personal lives, community lives work lives, that should be the goal of education. But it is not a commonly or broadly accepted goal. So for me we have to start by helping people understand the importance and the value of helping children develop as creative thinkers and why that is so important in today’s society.
12:56:43
	And that is sort of the why we need to change and we have to get a grip on why we need to change. Then there is the challenge of how we have to change, what are the changes we need to put in place in order to help reach that goal.  

Question	So what would you, if you could make a very short list of three changes, very simple changes in attitude or practical measures to educating not just children but people of any ages, their thinking about learning, what would they be?

Answer	When I think about the way I would like to see learning I sometimes think in terms of four guiding principles. They all begin with the letter P. Projects, passion, peers and play. So I think we need people of all ages, we need to give them opportunities to get actively involved in projects that are based on their passions in collaboration with peers in a playful spirit.  So I think all of those are important. Now working on a project is help people understand the creative process. When you work on a process you start with an idea, you try it out, some things don’t work, you revise it, you iterate, you adapt. So knowing that the process that goes into work on a project is key for people to develop as creative thinkers. But we can’t just tell people work on this project. We know that people are going to work longer and harder and be persistent in the face of challenges if they work on things they care about deeply. Things they are passionate about. So we always have to try to find peoples passions and let them build on their interests and build on their passions because we know they are going to be more motivated. But also we have seen them make deeper connections to ideas. If you are building on interests and you are making connections with ideas. If you just sort of are taught an idea you are forgetting the future.  If you encounter that idea when working on a project you are passionate about, you make a deeper connection to the idea.

	But we also know that learning is not an individual or solitary process.  A lot of times people get the wrong idea about thinking about the great Rodas sculpture of The Thinker. It is a great sculpture, but not a great model of the learning process about with a thinking process. Of course we do some of our thinking and learning in solitary deep contemplation and that is an important one element. But to be honest most creative learning happens in collaboration with other people and collaboration with other things. So we need to make sure we create environments where people are learning with and from others, where they are engaged with other people, get feedback and suggestions on what they have done. To get inspiration from other people where other people meet and from the projects from other people.

13:01:01	And then working on those projects, we think it is important for people to do it in a playful spirit.  And some of this is misunderstood. When people think of play they just think of laughing and having fun.  And there is nothing wrong with laughing and having fun. But for me play is not an activity it is more of an attitude.  It is an attitude we are constantly experimenting and trying new things and taking risks. And if you are going to be creative you need to be able to playfully experiment and try new things. So we have to create an environment where people feel safe and comfortable to experiment and take risks and be able to play. So it is not just a matter of playing a game, but being able to feel comfortable and confident in trying new things and comfortable when things go wrong. And seeing as a failure can be turned into an opportunity to say this gives a new idea. I can adapt that and go in new directions.  So projects, passion, peers and play for me is like a set of guiding principles for how we should start rethinking things.  

	And while we try to apply this to everything for creating a new space for learning, we think how could it support projects, passion, peers and play?  If we are developing a new technology we think about how can the technology support projects, passion, peers and play. Because too often as new technologies get introduced to the world, they get introduced in a way that aligns with the old vision of education and learning. If education was traditionally see as a way of delivering education from teacher to student, if people think, oh if technology could deliver information to the student. So you just take the teacher out put the technology there and it delivers information.  

	But that approach to learning is not what we need today. So we have a very, very vision of the way we should use new technologies. I want to see new digital technologies used in the same spirit as the wooden blocks and finger paint of kindergarten.  Technology should be a way for children to design, create, experiment and explore just the way they do with wooden blocks and finger paint.

Question	So the material of the technology, whether it is wooden blocks and finger paint or laptop is secondary to the material of I will give you four other words that just came up to me as you were speaking. Wonder, curiosity, trust and joy. So that is the material. And then the technology whatever it is, is secondary to that?

Answer	Yes so it is not only the nature of the activity and the nature of the engagement, not the materials, but more the nature of acidity and engagement. So the words you chose, joy, wonder, curiosity are all part of the nature of engagement.  And I do think that is what we need to be focused on.  And in some ways children will have a joyful experience building with blocks, they can also have a joyful experience creating new animation on a screen. So I am happy to embrace all of those things. Also they can have a not very creative experience with a person delivering information or a computer delivering information and both can be negative experiences.
13:05:58
Question	Or they can have a negative experience with somebody holding a lesson in a slightly autocratic way with finger paints and building blocks?

Answer	Yes right. So the material does not dictate exactly how it is going to be used.  Of course some materials are better designed to support creative activity and engagement and exploration, experimentation. But they all can be misused as well. So we should still design the technologies and materials and media to support and make more likely that they get used for designing, creating and experimenting and exploring. But we can also be designing activity structures and designing environments so it is not just about the materials or technologies, but designing activities, designing environments and designing facilitation approaches for the people around to know how to support the kids and using these materials in a creative way.

Female	Let’s walk up and look at Lego, never a bad thing.
